Then you are divorced one and one, so if she enters, one falls; if he delays the condition, then two fall. The obligating [factor]: His statement: (If you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one, so if she enters, one falls; if he delays the condition, then two falls) by him saying: You are divorced one and one if you enter the house, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two [companions] said: Two falls in both. And it was attributed to Abu Hanifa the statement that the waw indicates sequence, taken from his statement of the occurrence of one when the condition is advanced; because if it were for conjunction, all would be attached, and this is not correct. Rather, he said one because for him the later is attached by means of the former, so they descend accordingly, thus the first precedes and its speech is invalidated ... and the summary is that the letters are three, each with two aspects: advancing the condition and delaying it. So regarding fa and waw, one falls if he advances it, and two if he delays it. And regarding thumma, if he advances the condition, the first attaches, the second becomes effective, and the third is invalid; and if he delays it, the first becomes effective and what follows is invalid. And it is restricted to the conjunctive letter because it is mentioned without conjunction at all, such as: If you enter the house, then you are divorced one one one; so in Fath al-Qadir, one falls by agreement upon occurrence of the condition, and what follows is invalid due to the absence of anything requiring partnership.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding conditional divorce. The matn states a scenario: if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced one and one' (using the conjunction 'wa') and then she enters the house, one divorce falls. If he delays the condition by saying 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house', then two divorces fall. The commentator explains that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that two divorces fall in both scenarios. The author then delves into the underlying reasoning: Abu Hanifa's view is based on the interpretation of 'wa' as indicating sequence (tartib), so the first pronouncement attaches to the condition first and invalidates the second. The companions interpret 'wa' as indicating simultaneity (ma'iyyah), so both pronouncements attach together. The commentary cites Fath al-Qadir, which suggests the companions' view is stronger. The discussion continues to compare other conjunctions: 'fa' (which indicates immediate sequence) and 'thumma' (which indicates delayed sequence), and the effect of advancing or delaying the condition. The summary states that for 'fa' and 'wa', if the condition is advanced, one divorce falls; if delayed, two. For 'thumma', if the condition is advanced, the first attaches, the second becomes effective (if it is a new condition), and the third is void; if the condition is delayed, only the first becomes effective. The passage also notes a restrictive point: when divorce is uttered without any conjunction (e.g., 'you are divorced one one one' without 'wa'), according to Fath al-Qadir, only one divorce falls upon the condition, and the rest are void because there is nothing to link them together.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and' – in this context debated whether it indicates sequence or simultaneity.
تقديم الشرط (taqdim al-shart): Advancing the condition before the divorced pronouncement (e.g., 'If you enter, you are divorced').
تأخير الشرط (ta'khir al-shart): Delaying the condition after the divorced pronouncement (e.g., 'You are divorced if you enter').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes Abu Hanifa's reasoning for ruling only one divorce when the condition precedes in a 'wa' sentence?
A) 'Wa' literally means sequence, so the second divorce cannot occur after the first.
B) The second pronouncement attaches to the condition through the first, so when the first falls, the second cannot fall.
C) The condition is invalid because it comes first.
D) The wife is not yet divorced when the condition occurs.

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce with 'wa', Abu Hanifa differentiates based on the order of condition and pronouncement, while the Sahibayn rule two divorces regardless; Fath al-Qadir favors the Sahibayn.

The Reasoning and Other Conjunctions in Conditional Divorce
Expansion of ta'lil and rules for fa/thumma in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the principle of ta'alliq bi al-wasita and state the rules for 'fa' and 'thumma' in conditional divorce, including the case without conjunction.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's ta'lil: the later divorce attaches through the earlier; 'fa' gives immediate sequence, 'thumma' delay, and no conjunction disallows multiple divorces.

This lesson delves deeper into the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's position on conditional divorce, specifically the principle that a later pronouncement attaches to the condition by means of an earlier one. It then extends to other conjunctions: 'fa' (indicating immediate sequence) and 'thumma' (indicating delay), and the special case where divorce is repeated without any conjunction. Understanding these nuances is crucial for accurate fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of ta'alliq bi al-wasita
According to the passage, when a man says 'If you enter, you are divorced one and one', the second 'one' attaches to the condition via the first 'one'. This means the second is dependent on the first's attachment.
This principle is key to understanding why only one divorce falls in Abu Hanifa's view when the condition precedes.
2
Apply to the case of condition advanced
If the condition precedes, the first pronouncement attaches to the condition. The second attaches via the first. When the condition occurs, the first falls, and the wife becomes separated, so the second cannot fall because its basis (the first attachment) is gone.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn see all pronouncements as attaching directly to the condition simultaneously. Therefore, when the condition occurs, both fall together, regardless of order.
The difference is in the model of attachment.
4
Examine the rule for 'fa'
For 'fa' (immediate sequence), the passage says that if the condition is advanced, one divorce falls by agreement (اتفاقاً). This is because 'fa' indicates immediate sequence, so the first pronouncement is the only one that takes effect before the separation.
No dispute here.
5
Examine the rule for 'thumma'
For 'thumma' (delay), the passage gives: if condition advanced, the first attaches and becomes effective, the second becomes effective (if it can), and the third is invalid; if condition delayed, only the first becomes effective and the rest are invalid.
The delay inherent in 'thumma' affects the order of attachment.

Source Text

عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يقع ثنتان فيهما ونسب لأبي حنيفة القول بأن الواو للترتيب أخذاً من قوله بوقوع الواحدة فيما إذا قدم الشرط لأنها لو كانت للجمع لتعلق الكل وليس بصحيح، بل إنما قال بالواحدة لأن هذا عنده تعلق المتأخر بواسطة المتقدم فينزلن كذلك فيسبق الأول فتبطل الكلام محليتها وتوضيحه أن الأول تعلق قبل الثاني لعدم ما يوجب توقفه وتعلق الثاني بواسطته، والثالث بواسطتهما فينزل على الوجه الذي وقع عليه التعليق بخلاف ما إذا كرر الشرط لأن تعلق الثاني بغير شرط الأول ليس بواسطة الأول لأن كلاً جملة مستقلة فتعلق بالشرط الواحد طلقات ليس شيء منها بواسطة شيء فينزلن جميعاً عند الشرط بخلاف ما إذا أخر الشرط لأن تأخره موجب لتوقف الأول لأنه مغير فتعلق الكل به دفعة فينزل دفعة. ونسب إليهما القول بأنها للمعية أخذاً من قولهما بوقوع الثنتين وليس بصحيح، بل قالا بعدما اشتركت في التعلق بواسطة أن تنزل دفعة لأن نزول كل حكم الشرط فتقترن أحكامه كما في تعدد الشرط. قال في فتح القدير، قولهما أرجح وقول الإمام تعلق الثاني بواسطة تعلق الأول؛ إن أريد أنه علة فممنوع بل علته جمع الواو إياه أي الشرط، وإن أريد كونه سابق التعلق سلمناه ولا يفيد كالأيمان المتعاقبة، ولو سلم أن تعلق الأول علة لتعلق الثاني لم يلزم كون نزوله علة لنزوله إذ لا تلازم فجاز كونه علة لتعلقه فيتقدم في التعلق وليس نزوله علة لنزوله بل إذا تعلق الثاني بأي سبب كأن صار الأول متعلقين بشرط وعند نزول الشرط ينزل المشروط مع اهـ. وهذا كله تقرير الأصول وأما تقرير الفروع فوجه قول الإمام أن المعلق بالشرط كالمنجز عند وجوده ولو نجزه حقيقة لم يقع الثانية بخلاف ما إذا أخر الشرط لوجود المغير . كذا ذكر الشارح وحاصل ما في الهداية أن الواو لمطلق الجمع لا تصدق إلا في ضمن معية أو ترتيب، فعلى اعتبار المعية يقع الكل، وعلى اعتبار الترتيب لا يقع إلا واحدة فلا يقع الزائد بالشك وهو أقرب ماوجه به قول الإمام قيد بالواو لأنه لو عطف بالفاء وقدم الشرط وقعت واحدة اتفاقاً على الأصح للتعقيب ولو عطف بـ«ثم وأخر الشرط وقعت واحدة منجزة ولغا ما بعدها، وإن كانت مدخولاً بها تعلق الأخير وتنجز ما قبله وإن تقدم الشرط تعلق الأول وتنجز الثاني فيقع المعلق عند الشرط بعد التزوج الثاني ولغا الثالث وفي المدخول بها تعلق الأول ونجز ما بعده، وعندهما تعلق الكل بالشرط قدمه أو أخره إلا عند وجود الشرط تطلق تعلقه من شرح الفارسي قوله : (كالإيمان) (المتعاقبة قال الرملي : تفسيره لو قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق ثم بعد زمان قال إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق فدخلت يقع الكل اتفاقاً. قوله: (ولو عطف يتم وأخر الشرط الخ) قال الرملي : هذا غلط بلا شبهة ولا صحة لهذا كتاب الطلاق فصل في الطلاق قبل الدخول المدخول بها ثلاثاً وغيرها واحدة بناء على أن أثر التراخي يظهر في التعليق عنده فكأنه سكت بين كل كلمتين، وعندهما يظهر في الوقوع عند نزول الشرط لا في التعليق. والحاصل أن الحروف ثلاثة، وكل على وجهين تقديم الشرط وتأخيره. ففي الفاء والواو يقع واحدة إن قدمه واثنتان إن أخره. وفي «ثم» إن قدم الشرط تعلق الأول وتنجز الثاني ولغا الثالث، وإن أخره تنجز الأول ولغا ما بعده وقيد بحرف العطف لأنه ما ذكر بغير عطف أصلاً نحو إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة واحدة واحدة ففي فتح القدير يقع واحدة اتفاقاً عند وجود الشرط ويلغو ما بعده لعدم ما يوجب التشريك .
Then you are divorced one and one, so if she enters, one falls; if he delays the condition, then two fall. The obligating [factor]: His statement: (If you enter the house, then you are divorced one and one, so if she enters, one falls; if he delays the condition, then two falls) by him saying: You are divorced one and one if you enter the house, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two [companions] said: Two falls in both. And it was attributed to Abu Hanifa the statement that the waw indicates sequence, taken from his statement of the occurrence of one when the condition is advanced; because if it were for conjunction, all would be attached, and this is not correct. Rather, he said one because for him the later is attached by means of the former, so they descend accordingly, thus the first precedes and its speech is invalidated ... and the summary is that the letters are three, each with two aspects: advancing the condition and delaying it. So regarding fa and waw, one falls if he advances it, and two if he delays it. And regarding thumma, if he advances the condition, the first attaches, the second becomes effective, and the third is invalid; and if he delays it, the first becomes effective and what follows is invalid. And it is restricted to the conjunctive letter because it is mentioned without conjunction at all, such as: If you enter the house, then you are divorced one one one; so in Fath al-Qadir, one falls by agreement upon occurrence of the condition, and what follows is invalid due to the absence of anything requiring partnership.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expanding on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding conditional divorce. The matn states a scenario: if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced one and one' (using the conjunction 'wa') and then she enters the house, one divorce falls. If he delays the condition by saying 'You are divorced one and one if you enter the house', then two divorces fall. The commentator explains that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that two divorces fall in both scenarios. The author then delves into the underlying reasoning: Abu Hanifa's view is based on the interpretation of 'wa' as indicating sequence (tartib), so the first pronouncement attaches to the condition first and invalidates the second. The companions interpret 'wa' as indicating simultaneity (ma'iyyah), so both pronouncements attach together. The commentary cites Fath al-Qadir, which suggests the companions' view is stronger. The discussion continues to compare other conjunctions: 'fa' (which indicates immediate sequence) and 'thumma' (which indicates delayed sequence), and the effect of advancing or delaying the condition. The summary states that for 'fa' and 'wa', if the condition is advanced, one divorce falls; if delayed, two. For 'thumma', if the condition is advanced, the first attaches, the second becomes effective (if it is a new condition), and the third is void; if the condition is delayed, only the first becomes effective. The passage also notes a restrictive point: when divorce is uttered without any conjunction (e.g., 'you are divorced one one one' without 'wa'), according to Fath al-Qadir, only one divorce falls upon the condition, and the rest are void because there is nothing to link them together.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic conjunction 'and' – in this context debated whether it indicates sequence or simultaneity.
تقديم الشرط (taqdim al-shart): Advancing the condition before the divorced pronouncement (e.g., 'If you enter, you are divorced').
تأخير الشرط (ta'khir al-shart): Delaying the condition after the divorced pronouncement (e.g., 'You are divorced if you enter').
ثم (thumma): The Arabic conjunction 'then', indicating delay.
الفاء (al-fa): The Arabic conjunction 'so' or 'then', indicating immediate sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a conditional divorce using 'fa' when the condition is advanced?
A) Two divorces fall, with disagreement.
B) One divorce falls by agreement.
C) Three divorces fall.
D) The divorce is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The ruling for 'fa' and 'thumma' in conditional divorce depends on their temporal meaning; the case without conjunction results in only one divorce by agreement.

Combining Talaq, Zihar, and Ila in One Conditional Statement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining talaq, zihar, and ila in one conditional sentence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the effect of combining talaq, zihar, and ila in a single conditional statement, and apply the rule of precedence (sabq) to determine which acts take effect.

Core Idea
The first valid marital dissolution act in a sequence nullifies the rest.

Sometimes a husband may utter a single conditional sentence that includes a divorce, a zihar declaration, and an oath of ila all at once. What happens when the condition is fulfilled? Do all three take effect, or only the first? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq, presents the Hanafi position and highlights an important intra-madhhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two cases: (1) the husband says the condition to his non-consummated wife, and (2) he says it to an ajnabiyyah (a woman not yet married to him) before marrying her. Identify the key difference in who is addressed.
2
Determine the sequence of statements
In each scenario, note the order in which talaq, zihar, and ila are mentioned. The order determines the ruling because the first valid act takes effect and removes the wife’s legal capacity for subsequent acts.
In the first scenario, the husband says: ‘If you enter, you are divorced, you are to me like my mother’s back, and by Allah I will not approach you.’ Talaq comes first.
3
Apply Abu Hanifa’s rule of precedence
Abu Hanifa holds that when talaq is pronounced first, it takes effect immediately upon fulfillment of the condition, dissolving the marriage. The wife then ceases to be a wife, so zihar and ila cannot occur. If ila comes before talaq (as in the second scenario when zihar and ila are advanced), ila takes effect first, then zihar, then talaq.
4
Apply the Sahibayn’s simultaneous-effect view
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider that all three acts are simultaneously initiated when the condition is fulfilled. Thus, the husband is a divorcer, a muzahir, and a muli—all rulings apply.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, only one dissolution act occurs; under the Sahibayn, all three are considered. The later Hanafi position leans towards the Sahibayn’s view in many cases, but the passage does not explicitly tarjih.
The passage ends with “So it is in Fath al-Qadir,” indicating the view is documented, not necessarily the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو قال لغير المدخولة إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق وأنت علي كظهر أمي والله لا أقربك فدخلت طلقت وسقط الظهار والإيلاء عنده لسبق الطلاق فتبين فلا تبقى محلاً لما بعده. وعندهما هو مطلق مظاهر مول وإلى أنه لو قال لأجنبية إن تزوجتك فأنت طالق وأنت علي كظهر أمي ووالله لا أقربك وتزوجها، فعلى الخلاف بخلاف ما لو قدم الظهار والإيلاء وقع الكل عند الكل. أما عندهما فظاهر، وأما عنده فلسبق الإيلاء. ثم هي بعده محل للظهار، ثم هي بعدهما محل للطلاق فتطلق كذا في فتح القدير.
And the author indicated that if he says to a non-consummated [wife]: If you enter the house, then you are divorced, and you are to me like my mother's back, and by Allah I will not approach you, and she enters, then she is divorced and the zihar and ila are dropped according to him (Abu Hanifa) due to the precedence of divorce, so she becomes separated, thus she does not remain a locus for what follows. And according to the two [companions], he is a divorcer, a muzahir, and a muli. And that if he says to a non-marriageable woman: If I marry you, then you are divorced, and you are to me like my mother's back, and by Allah I will not approach you, and he marries her, then according to the difference [of opinion], contrary to if he advanced the zihar and ila, everything falls according to all. As for according to the two, it is apparent; and as for according to him (Abu Hanifa), due to the precedence of ila. Then she after it is a locus for zihar, and after both of them a locus for divorce, so she is divorced. So it is in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a husband combines divorce (talaq), zihar (declaring his wife like his mother's back), and ila (vowing to abstain from intercourse) in one conditional statement towards his wife. The author of the commentary points out two cases: first, when the man says to his non-consummated wife (غير المدخولة) 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, you are to me like my mother's back, and by Allah I will not approach you.' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when she enters, the divorce occurs first and takes effect immediately, dissolving the marriage. Since she becomes separated, she can no longer be subject to zihar or ila, so those are dropped. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), all three acts are considered to have been initiated simultaneously, so the man is considered a divorcer, a muzahir, and a muli (i.e., the rulings of all apply). The second case involves an ajnabiyyah (a woman not married to him) when he says 'If I marry you, then you are divorced...' and then he marries her. Here there is a difference based on whether the zihar and ila are mentioned before or after the divorce. If the divorce is first, the ruling is as above. But if the man advances the zihar and ila (i.e., mentions them before the divorce), then all three fall according to both positions because the woman becomes a wife first, then she is subject to zihar and ila, and then divorce. This illustrates the principle that the sequence of statements and the legal capacity of the wife at each moment determine which acts take effect.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A declaration by the husband comparing his wife to his mother’s back, suspending marital relations until kaffarah is performed.
إيلاء (ila’): A vow by the husband to abstain from intercourse for four months or more; if he does not return, divorce occurs automatically.
غير المدخولة (ghayr al-madkhulah): A wife who has not been consummated with; considered not fully a wife in some contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says to his non-consummated wife ‘If you enter the house, you are divorced, and you are to me like my mother’s back, and by Allah I will not approach you,’ and she enters, what do the Sahibayn rule?
A) She is divorced and the zihar and ila are dropped.
B) He is a divorcer, a muzahir, and a muli (all acts take effect).
C) Only the zihar and ila take effect because divorce is invalid with zihar.
D) The condition is invalid because it combines too many statements.

Key Takeaway
When combining talaq, zihar, and ila in one conditional statement, the first valid dissolution act that removes the wife’s capacity (talaq) nullifies the rest according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn hold that all three take effect simultaneously.

Multiple Talaq Pronouncements with Conjunctions in Conditional Divorce
Rulings on multiple talaq with conjunctions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi school distinguishes between different formulations of multiple divorce pronouncements in conditional statements and apply the correct number of divorces that fall.

Core Idea
The placement and conjunction of 'talaq' determine whether one or three divorces occur under a condition.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines how multiple divorce pronouncements interact with conditional clauses. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes based on the conjunctive particle used (wa, thumma, fa) and the order of words. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for determining the number of divorces that actually take effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the formulation and condition placement
Read the entire conditional statement. Note whether the condition (e.g., 'if I marry you') comes before or after the divorce pronouncements, and whether the pronouncements are separated by conjunctions (wa, thumma) or no conjunction.
Example: 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced on the day I marry you' – condition at end with wa.
2
Determine the effect of the conjunction
Apply the Hanafi rule: When multiple pronouncements are linked by 'wa', they are considered separate and each can be either conditional or immediate depending on the order. If the condition precedes all, all are conditional; if it follows, only the first is conditional? Actually, as per the text, when condition is after, all three are conditional and three fall. When condition is before, only first is conditional and the rest void.
The passage: 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced and divorced and divorced' – one falls. Reverse – three fall.
3
Examine the exception with 'thumma'
When using 'thumma' (then), the first pronouncement becomes effective immediately, the second attaches conditionally (if the condition is expressed with it), and the third is void if not attached.
Example: 'You are divorced, then divorced if I marry you, then divorced' – first effective, second conditional, third void.
4
Consider the state of the wife and variant readings
For pronouncements without conjunction, the text from al-Bazzaziyyah distinguishes between a non-consummated and consummated wife. In the non-consummated case, the first is conditional, the second descends immediately, third void. In the consummated case, all three descend.
This shows the importance of the wife's marital status (madkhul biha vs. ghair madkhul biha).
5
Account for the opinion of Zufar
Zufar holds that if the condition is mentioned once before repeated pronouncements, the second and third are void because they are conditioned on the same condition. The Hanafi position (us) is that the repetition itself is a new condition, so all are effective.
The text: 'But according to Zufar, it is by the condition, so if he limited, the second is void; and according to us, it is by the condition, so it is established.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلى أنه لو قال لامرأة يوم أتزوجك فأنت طالق وطالق وطالق فتزوجها وقعت واحدة وبطلت الثنتان، ولو قال أنت طالق وطالق وطالق يوم أتزوجك وقعت الثلاث كذا في الحاوي القدسي. وكذا لو قال إن تزوجتك كما في المحيط وفي تلخيص الجامع من أول كتاب الأيمان : لو قال ثلاثاً لغير المدخولة إن كلمتك فأنت طالق انحلت الأولى بالثانية لاستئناف الكلام بخلاف فاذهبي يا عدوة الله، لكن عند زفر بالشرط كما لو اقتصر فلغت الثانية وعندنا بالجزاء فانعقدت إذ الكلام إلا لو كان التعليق بقوله أنت طالق ثم طالق إن تزوجتك ثم طالق فإنه حينئذ يتنجز الأول ويتعلق الثاني ويلغو الثالث لأن بقوله أنت طالق وقع الطلاق وبقوله ثم طالق إن تزوجتك تطلق بالتزوج المعلق عليه الطلاق ولغا الثالث لعدم الإضافة إلى التزوج فتأمل وانظر إلى قوله «والحاصل أن الحروف ثلاثة إلى آخره» ا هـ . وهذا الاعتراض مبني على ما وقع له من نسخة سقيمة وهي : ولو عطف بثم وأخر الشرط تعلق الثاني وتنجز الأول فيقع المعلق عند الشرط بعد التزوج الثاني ولغا الثالث، وفي المدخول بها تعلق الأول وتنجز ما عبده. وعلى ما في عامة النسخ لا اعتراض بل هو الموافق لما في الفتح والتبيين والنهر وغيرها قوله : ( وقيد بحرف العطف الخ) في إيمان البزازية من الثالث في يمين الطلاق إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق طالق طالق وهي غير ملموسة، فالأول معلق بالشرط، والثاني ينزل في الحال ويلغو الثالث، وإن تزوجها ودخل الدار نزل المعلق ولو دخل بعد البينونة قبل التزوج انحل اليمين لا إلى جزاء ولو موطوءة تعلق الأول ونزل الثاني والثالث في اهـ. وهذا كما ترى مخالف لما نقله هنا عن الفتح إلا أن يفرق بين واحدة واحدة وبين طالق طالق وهو الظاهر قوله : (بخلاف فاذهبي يا عدوة الله لأن ذكره بفاء العطف يقتضي تعلقه بما سبق فصار الحال
And that if he says to a woman: On the day I marry you, you are divorced and divorced and divorced, and he marries her, one falls and the two are void. And if he says: You are divorced and divorced and divorced on the day I marry you, three fall. So it is in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. And similarly if he says: If I marry you, as in al-Muhit. And in Talkhis al-Jami' from the beginning of the Book of Oaths: If he says thrice to a non-consummated woman: If I speak to you, then you are divorced; the first is dissolved by the second because the speech is resumed, contrary to 'Go, O enemy of Allah.' But according to Zufar, it is by the condition, so if he limited, the second is void; and according to us, it is by the condition, so it is established when the speech [is spoken?]. Except if the attachment is by his saying: You are divorced, then divorced if I marry you, then divorced; then at that time the first becomes effective, the second attaches, and the third is void because by his saying 'you are divorced' divorce occurred, and by his saying 'then divorced if I marry you' she is divorced upon the marriage on which the divorce is conditioned, and the third is void due to lack of connection to the marriage. So reflect and look at his statement 'And the summary is that the letters are three, etc.' end quote. And this objection is based on what occurred to him from a defective copy, namely: And if he connects with thumma and delays the condition, the second attaches and the first becomes effective, so the conditioned occurs upon the condition after the second marriage, and the third is void; and in the consummated [wife], the first attaches and what is after becomes effective. But according to the majority of copies, there is no objection, rather it agrees with what is in al-Fath, al-Tabyin, al-Nahr, and others. His statement: (And restricted by the conjunctive letter etc.) In Ayman al-Bazzaziyyah from the third section on divorce oaths: If he says: If you enter the house, then you are divorced, divorced, divorced, and she is not touched, then the first is conditioned on the condition, the second descends immediately, and the third is void. And if he marries her and enters the house, the conditioned descends. And if he enters after separation before marriage, the oath dissolves without a consequence. And if she is a touched [wife], the first attaches and the second and third descend. This, as you see, contradicts what he transmitted here from al-Fath, unless one distinguishes between 'one one' and 'divorced divorced', which is apparent. His statement: (Contrary to 'Go, O enemy of Allah' because mentioning it with the conjunction fa requires its attachment to what preceded, so the state is...
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of conditional divorce with multiple pronouncements. It presents several scenarios: If a man says to a woman 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced and divorced and divorced' (using 'wa' between them) and then marries her, only one divorce falls because the first divorce occurs upon marriage and the rest are void. If he reverses the order ('You are divorced and divorced and divorced on the day I marry you'), three divorces fall because the condition applies to all three. Similarly, the author quotes from al-Hawi al-Qudsi and al-Muhit. The passage then cites a more complex case from Talkhis al-Jami': if a man says thrice to a non-consummated wife 'If I speak to you, then you are divorced', the first pronouncement is annulled by the second because the speech is resumed (so only the last applies), but this is unlike the phrase 'Go, O enemy of Allah' which would be a separate speech. However, according to Zufar, it operates by the condition, so if he mentions the condition once, only the first applies; but according to the Hanafis (us), it operates by the condition, so all are effective. The text then discusses exceptions: if the attachment uses 'thumma' and the condition is delayed, the first becomes effective and the second attaches, etc. It also notes a variant reading from al-Bazzaziyyah regarding 'If you enter the house, then you are divorced, divorced, divorced' (without 'wa'): the first is conditioned, the second descends immediately (as an unconditional divorce), and the third is void. A distinction is proposed between saying 'one one' (واحدة واحدة) and 'divorced divorced' (طالق طالق) – the latter may treat each as independent. The passage ends with an incomplete comment about 'Go, O enemy of Allah'.

Key Terms
حرف العطف (harf al-'ataf): Conjunctive particle (وَ, فَ, ثُمَّ) that links divorce pronouncements and affects whether they occur together or separately.
المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها (al-madkhul biha wa ghayr al-madkhul biha): Consummated wife vs. non-consummated wife – the ruling on immediate pronouncements differs based on this status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'You are divorced and divorced and divorced on the day I marry you' (using 'wa'), and he marries her, how many divorces fall according to the passage?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The number of divorces in a conditional statement depends on the placement of the condition, the conjunctions used, and the consummation status of the wife.

Effect of Conjunctions in Conditional Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of conjunctions in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of divorces that occur for each conjunction (fa, waw, thumma) in conditional divorce according to Abu Hanifa, and explain the difference with the Sahibayn's principle.

Core Idea
The conjunction and word order in conditional divorce determine the number of divorces that take effect.

This lesson examines the effect of the conjunctions fa, waw, and thumma in conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq). A husband's choice of wording—whether he places the condition before or after the divorce pronouncements, and which conjunction he uses—can change the number of divorces that occur. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on the underlying principle, leading to practical differences in the outcomes. Understanding these rules is crucial for correctly determining the number of divorces that take effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conjunction and word order
Determine whether the husband uses fa, waw, thumma, or no conjunction, and whether the condition comes before or after the divorce pronouncements.
2
Apply Abu Hanifa's rule for fa and waw
If the condition is first: one divorce occurs. If the condition is last: two divorces occur.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
3
Apply the rule for thumma
If condition first: the first divorce is suspended, the second becomes effective immediately, the third is void. If condition last: the first becomes effective immediately, and the rest are void.
There is no dispute on thumma; both imams agree.
4
Note the case without a conjunction
If the husband repeats the divorce pronouncement without any conjunction (e.g., 'one, one, one'), only one divorce occurs upon fulfillment of the condition.
This is by agreement as per Fath al-Qadir.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa bases his ruling on the principle that delay (tarakhi) appears in the ta'liq itself, so subsequent pronouncements are absorbed into the first. The Sahibayn hold that delay appears at the time of occurrence, so each conjunction creates a separate ta'liq.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق فصل في الطلاق قبل الدخول

المدخول بها ثلاثاً وغيرها واحدة بناء على أن أثر التراخي يظهر في التعليق عنده فكأنه سكت بين كل كلمتين، وعندهما يظهر في الوقوع عند نزول الشرط لا في التعليق. والحاصل أن الحروف ثلاثة، وكل على وجهين تقديم الشرط وتأخيره. ففي الفاء والواو يقع واحدة إن قدمه واثنتان إن أخره. وفي «ثم» إن قدم الشرط تعلق الأول وتنجز الثاني ولغا الثالث، وإن أخره تنجز الأول ولغا ما بعده وقيد بحرف العطف لأنه ما ذكر بغير عطف أصلاً نحو إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق واحدة واحدة واحدة ففي فتح القدير يقع واحدة اتفاقاً عند وجود الشرط ويلغو ما بعده لعدم ما يوجب التشريك.
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Divorce Before Consummation. The one with whom marriage was consummated [gets] three, and other than her [gets] one, based on the fact that the effect of delay appears in the ta'liq according to him [Abu Hanifa], as if he paused between every two words. According to them [the Sahibayn], it appears in the occurrence at the descent of the condition, not in the ta'liq. The summary is that the letters are three, and each has two aspects: putting the condition first and putting it last. With fa and waw, one [divorce] occurs if he puts it first, and two if he puts it last. With thumma, if he puts the condition first, the first [divorce] is suspended, the second becomes effective immediately, and the third is void. If he puts it last, the first becomes effective immediately and what follows is void. And it is restricted to a conjunction because if it is mentioned without any conjunction at all, like 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, one, one, one', then in Fath al-Qadir, one divorce occurs by agreement upon the existence of the condition, and what follows is void because there is nothing that requires joining.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the effect of different conjunctions in conditional divorce (talaq mu'allaq). The core issue is whether the condition is stated before or after the divorce pronouncement and which conjunction is used. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the delay (tarakhi) manifests in the ta'liq (suspension) itself, so when a man says to his wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and you are divorced, and you are divorced' using 'wa' or 'fa', the second and third are considered suspended along with the first if the condition is stated first, but if the condition is stated last, the first divorce becomes immediate and the subsequent ones are also immediate but subject to the condition? Actually the text says: with fa and waw, one divorce occurs if he puts the condition first (meaning the condition is mentioned before the divorce pronouncements), and two if he puts it last (meaning the divorce pronouncements are mentioned first, then the condition). This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the delay affects the occurrence at the descent of the condition, not the ta'liq. The three conjunctions are fa, waw, and thumma. For fa and waw, the ruling is as above. For thumma, if the condition is stated first, the first divorce is suspended (ta'allaqa), the second becomes effective immediately (tanajjaza), and the third is void (lagha). If the condition is stated last, the first divorce becomes effective immediately and what follows is void. The author then mentions that if the divorce is mentioned without any conjunction at all, like repeating 'one, one, one' after the condition, then according to Fath al-Qadir, only one divorce occurs upon the condition, and the rest are void because there is no connector to make them part of the same sentence. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa as it is the basis of the school, though the Sahibayn's view is also considered in some contexts.

Key Terms
حروف العطف (huruf al-'ataf): Conjunctions that connect words or phrases; here specifically fa, waw, and thumma used in conditional divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his non-consummated wife 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and you are divorced, and you are divorced' (using 'wa'), how many divorces occur according to Abu Hanifa?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The conjunction and word order in conditional divorce determine the number of divorces that take effect; Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position.

Combined Divorce, Zihar, and Ila' in a Conditional Statement
Discusses combined conditional divorce with zihar and ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man combines divorce, zihar, and ila' in one conditional statement, and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the effect of a prior divorce.

Core Idea
In a combined conditional, a prior divorce nullifies subsequent zihar and ila' according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a scenario where a husband issues three separate legal acts—divorce, zihar, and ila'—in a single conditional statement. The ruling hinges on whether the divorce takes effect first, removing the wife as a legal subject for the subsequent acts. We will examine the Hanafi positions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal acts are being combined and what the Hanafi school rules regarding their validity. Here, divorce, zihar, and ila' are all conditional upon entry into the house.
The key question is whether all three take effect or some are nullified.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on the principle that divorce immediately separates the wife, making her no longer a valid subject for zihar or ila'. The text cites Fath al-Qadir as authority.
No direct Quran or Hadith is quoted; the reasoning is talil (legal cause).
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that zihar and ila' are dropped because the divorce precedes and removes her as a wife. The Sahibayn hold that all three are valid because they are simultaneous.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text indicates that if zihar and ila' are placed first, all three occur by consensus. This suggests that the order matters, and the majority view aligns with Abu Hanifa's reasoning in the original scenario.
The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here, but later reliance on the majority indicates preference.

الجملة واحدة وإلا نزل اثنان على المدخولة بتكرير كلما كلمتك فأنت طالق وانحلت بالثانية لا إلى جراء ولغت هي بعدم الملك، وفي إن حلفت بطلاقك لا تنحل اليمين الثانية إلا بتعليق طلاقها بالملك أو بعده إذ الشرط إدخالها في الجزاء. كذا في تعليق طلاقها ومدخولة بالحلف بطلاقهما إنما تنحل الثانية بتعليق طلاقها بالملك أو بعده إذ الثالثة انعقدت على المدخولة فكانت الثالثة شطر الشرط وذا في حق الثالثة شطر أيضاً فلا تنحل ما لم يحلف بطلاق المدخولة وهي البردعية ا.هـ. يعني أن هذه المسألة تلقب بالبردعية لأن أبا سعيد البردعي بعدما تفقه ودرس سئل عنها فلم يهتد إلى جوابها فارتحل إلى بغداد وتعلم سبع سنين حتى صار من كبار أصحابنا . وقيد بغير المدخولة لأن فيها يتعلق الكل بالشرط قدمه أو حسب

الكل كلاماً واحداً بخلاف ما لو لم يذكره بالفاء لكن انحلال اليمين الأولى في مسألتنا عند زفر بشرط الثانية وهو قوله إن كلمتك» لأن شرط الحنث مطلق الكلام وقد وجد فصار كما لو اقتصر عليه، ولم يتلفظ بالجزاء فيصادفها الجزاء وهي مبانة لا إلى عدة فلا تنعقد عليها اليمين الثانية وعند الثلاثة بالجزاء فانعقدت الثانية لأن الجملة الشرطية واحدة والمتعارف الكلام المفيد بخلاف ما لو اقتصر على الشرط لأن الكلام يكون تاماً وناقصاً، فإن اقتصر على الناقص علم أنه المراد، وإن جاوزه إلى التام على أنه المراد. وعلى اختيار ابن الفضل لا يحنث لو اقتصر وبه يندفع استشهاد زفر، ولأن الجملة لو لم تكن واحدة لنزل طلقتان على المدخولة بتكرير كلما طلقتك فأنت طالق لأن قوله ثانياً كلما طلقتك مخاطبة لها وكذلك فأنت طالق خطاب ثانٍ فإذا ثبت انعقاد اليمين الثانية انحلت . بوجود الثالثة لا إلى جزاء لأن الجزاء يصادفها وهي مبانة فتلغوا الثالثة لعدم الملك . وقال أبو مطيع وجماعة من مشايخ بلخ: لا ينحل منها شيء إلا بكلام مبتدأ وإليه سبق وهم أبي حنيفة حين سأله محمد في صغره عمن قال ثلاثاً والله لا أكلمك وقال يا شيخ انظر حسناً فقال : حنث مرتين فقال محمد: أحسنت. وقوله وفي إن حلفت «الخ أي وفيما لو قال ثلاث مرات لغير المدخولة إن حلفت بطلاقك فأنت طالق لا تنحل اليمين الثانية إلا بتعليق طلاقها بالملك بأن يقول إن تزوجتك فأنت طالق أو يتعلق بعد ملك النكاح بأن يتزوجها ويقول إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق لأن شرط الانحلال هنا هو الحلف بطلاقها وذلك بإدخالها في جزاء اليمين الثالثة وهو الطلاق، ولا يصح إدخالها فيه لعدم الملك عند وجودها بخلاف الأولى لأن الشرط وهو الكلام يتصور في غير الملك، وكذا الحكم في تعليق الرجل طلاق امرأتيه المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها بالحلف بطلاقيكما بأن قال لهما ثلاثاً إن حلفت بطلاقيكما فأنتما طالقان إنما تنحل الثانية في حقهما بتعليق طلاق غير المدخولة بالملك أو بعده بشرط آخر كما مر لأن اليمين الثالثة التي هي شرط انحلال الثانية إنما انعقد على المدخولة خاصة لأن الشرط في انحلال الثانية الحلف بطلاقهما وذلك بإدخالهما في جزاء الثالثة وهو الطلاق، ولم يمكن إدخال غير المدخولة فيه لعدم الملك كما فكانت الثالثة في حق انحلال الثانية شطر الشرط لا كله فلا يؤثر في انحلال شيء فإذا علق بعده طلاق غير المدخولة بالملك أو بعده بشرط آخر كمل الشرط فتطلق كل
And the author indicated that if he said to a non-consummated woman: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, and you are like my mother's back, and by Allah I will not approach you,' and she entered, she is divorced, and the zihar and ila' are dropped according to him [Abu Hanifa] because the divorce precedes, so she becomes separated and is no longer a place for what follows. According to them [the Sahibayn], he is a man who has made zihar and ila'. And that if he said to a foreign woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced, and you are like my mother's back, and by Allah I will not approach you,' and he marries her, then it is according to the difference. Unlike if he put zihar and ila' first, then everything occurs according to everyone. As for according to them, it is apparent, and as for according to him, because ila' precedes. Then she is after that a place for zihar, then she is after both a place for divorce, so she is divorced. So in Fath al-Qadir. And that if he said to a woman 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced,' and he marries her, one divorce occurs and the two become void. If he said 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced on the day I marry you,' three divorces occur. So in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. Similarly if he said 'If I marry you' as in al-Muhit. And in Talkhis al-Jami' from the beginning of Kitab al-Ayman: if he said three times to a non-consummated woman 'If I speak to you, you are divorced,' the first is dissolved by the second because of restarting speech, unlike 'Go, O enemy of Allah.' But according to Zufar, by the condition as if he confined himself, so the second is void. According to us [Hanafis], by the result, so it is concluded, except if the ta'liq is by his saying 'You are divorced, then divorced if I marry you, then divorced,' then at that time the first becomes effective immediately, the second is suspended, and the third is void because by his saying 'You are divorced' the divorce occurred, and by his saying 'then divorced if I marry you' she divorces upon the marriage that is the condition of the divorce, and the third is void because of lack of connection to the marriage. So reflect and look at his saying 'The summary is that the letters are three...' end. This objection is based on a defective copy he had, which says: and if he connects with thumma and delays the condition, the second is suspended and the first becomes effective, so the suspended occurs at the condition after the second marriage, and the third is void. In the case of a consummated woman, the first is suspended and what follows becomes effective. According to what is in most copies, there is no objection; rather it agrees with what is in al-Fath, al-Tabyin, al-Nahr, and others. His saying: (And it is restricted to a conjunction, etc.) In Ayman al-Bazzaziyya from the third chapter on oaths of divorce: if he says 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, divorced, divorced' and she is not touched, then the first is suspended by the condition, the second descends immediately, and the third is void. If he marries her and she enters the house, the suspended descends. If she enters after separation before marriage, the oath is dissolved without a result. If she is a consummated wife, the first is suspended and the second and third descend immediately. This, as you see, contradicts what he transmitted here from al-Fath, unless there is a difference between 'one, one, one' and 'divorced, divorced, divorced', which is apparent. His saying: (Unlike 'Go, O enemy of Allah' because mentioning it with the conjunction fa requires its connection to what preceded, so the sentence becomes one. Otherwise, two would descend upon a consummated woman if she repeats 'every time I speak to you, you are divorced,' and the second is dissolved without a result, and it becomes void due to lack of ownership. And in the case of 'If I swear by your divorce,' the second oath does not dissolve except by suspending her divorce upon ownership or after it, because the condition is her entry into the result. Similarly, in the suspension of her divorce, and a consummated woman by swearing by their divorce, the second dissolves only by suspending her divorce upon ownership or after it, because the third oath is concluded upon the consummated woman, so the third is a part of the condition, and this is also a part in the right of the third, so it does not dissolve until he swears by the divorce of the consummated woman. This is the Bardha'iyyah case, end. Meaning this case is called al-Bardha'iyyah because Abu Sa'id al-Bardha'i, after he became a jurist and taught, was asked about it and could not find its answer, so he traveled to Baghdad and studied for seven years until he became one of our great companions. And it is restricted to a non-consummated woman because in her case everything is suspended by the condition, whether he puts it first or last. The whole sentence is one, unlike if he did not mention it with fa. But the dissolution of the first oath in our case according to Zufar is by the condition of the second, which is his saying 'If I speak to you,' because the condition of the breach is absolute speech, and it has occurred, so it becomes as if he confined himself to it, and he did not utter the result, so the result encounters her while she is separated without a waiting period, so the second oath does not conclude upon her. According to the three [Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad], it is by the result, so the second is concluded because the conditional sentence is one, and the common usage is complete speech, unlike if he confined himself to the condition, because the speech is both complete and incomplete. If he confines himself to the incomplete, it is known that it is intended; if he goes beyond to the complete, it is intended. According to the choice of Ibn al-Fadl, he does not breach if he confines himself, and this refutes Zufar's argument. And because if the sentence were not one, then two divorces would descend upon a consummated woman by repeating 'every time I divorce you, you are divorced,' because his saying a second time 'every time I divorce you' is addressing her, and similarly 'you are divorced' is a second address. So if the conclusion of the second oath is established, it dissolves by the existence of the third without a result because the result encounters her while she is separated, so the third becomes void due to lack of ownership. Abu Muti' and a group of scholars from Balkh said: nothing dissolves from it except with a new utterance, and this was the opinion of Abu Hanifa when Muhammad asked him in his childhood about someone who said three times 'By Allah, I will not speak to you' and said 'O shaykh, look well,' so he said: he breaks twice. Muhammad said: well said. And his saying 'And in the case of 'If I swear' etc.' means: in the case of someone who said three times to a non-consummated woman 'If I swear by your divorce, you are divorced,' the second oath does not dissolve except by suspending her divorce upon ownership, such as saying 'If I marry you, you are divorced' or it is suspended after marriage by saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' because the condition of dissolution here is swearing by her divorce, and that is by her entry into the result of the third oath, which is divorce, and it is not valid to enter her into it due to lack of ownership at the time of its occurrence, unlike the first because the condition, which is speech, is conceivable without ownership. Similarly, the ruling in the case of a man suspending the divorce of his two wives, one consummated and one not, by swearing by their divorce, such as saying to them three times 'If I swear by your divorce, you are both divorced,' the second dissolves with respect to them only by suspending the divorce of the non-consummated woman upon ownership or after it with another condition, as passed, because the third oath, which is the condition of dissolution of the second, was concluded upon the consummated woman only, because the condition for dissolution of the second is swearing by their divorce, and that is by entering both into the result of the third, which is divorce, and it was not possible to enter the non-consummated woman into it due to lack of ownership, so the third, with respect to dissolution of the second, is part of the condition, not all of it, so it does not effect any dissolution. Then if he later suspends the divorce of the non-consummated woman upon ownership or after it with another condition, the condition is completed, so each divorces.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq covers multiple complex scenarios of conditional divorce, including the famous Bardha'iyyah case. The text begins by discussing a case where a man says to his non-consummated wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, you are like my mother's back (zihar), and by Allah I will not approach you (ila').' According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the divorce takes precedence, so the wife is divorced and becomes separated, and the zihar and ila' are nullified because she is no longer his wife. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is considered a man who has made both zihar and ila', meaning both are still valid. This difference arises because Abu Hanifa sees that the divorce, being immediate upon fulfillment of the condition, removes her from being a wife before zihar and ila' can take effect, while the Sahibayn view the combination as simultaneous. The text then mentions that if he marries a foreign woman and says the same, the same difference applies. However, if he put zihar and ila' first, then all three occur according to all scholars. Next, the text discusses a case where a man says to a woman 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced, and divorced, and divorced' (with 'wa'). If he marries her, only one divorce occurs and the other two are void because the condition (marriage) is mentioned only with the first 'taliq', and the subsequent ones are considered repetitive without a new condition. But if he says 'You are divorced, and divorced, and divorced on the day I marry you,' then all three occur upon marriage because the condition applies to all three. The Bardha'iyyah case is then introduced: it involves a man who says to his non-consummated wife three times 'If I speak to you, you are divorced.' The question is how many divorces occur and when. The text explains that according to Zufar, the first oath is dissolved by the second because the condition (speaking) has occurred, but the second oath is void because it encounters her while already divorced. According to the majority of Hanafis (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), the second oath is concluded because the conditional sentence is considered one complete unit, and the breach occurs upon speaking, so the first divorce takes effect, and the second oath is dissolved without a result because she is already divorced. The third is similarly void. The text also mentions the opinion of Ibn al-Fadl and Abu Muti'. The story of Abu Sa'id al-Bardha'i illustrates the difficulty of this case: he was a great scholar who was stumped by this question and had to study in Baghdad for seven years to find the answer, which led to the case being named after him. The passage then discusses other scenarios involving swearing by divorce and multiple wives. Throughout, the Hanafi position is that the structure of the sentence and the presence of conjunctions determine whether multiple oaths are considered one unit or separate. The relied-upon position in the school is that of the majority (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) as opposed to Zufar's view.

Key Terms
الظهار (al-zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are like my mother's back', which in Islam requires kaffarah before resuming relations.
الإيلاء (al-ila'): An oath to abstain from marital relations for a period; if the period passes without resumption, it leads to a judicial divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario from the lesson, what is the consensus when zihar and ila' are placed before the divorce in the conditional?
A) Only zihar and ila' occur, divorce is null.
B) All three occur.
C) Only divorce occurs.
D) None occur because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In a combined conditional, the first effective act (divorce) removes the subject, so subsequent acts (zihar, ila') are nullified according to Abu Hanifa.
